- **2025-05-05 11:09** *Jake Panzer*: Hi @Ingrid, we wanted to share this with you directly before looping in the broader email thread with the Google reps. In short, we don't recommend scaling too much further in this time, given where we are at with efficiency. Often, we find reps try to push the limits of spend, so wanted to share the numbers below:  
  
â€¢ Last year (Apr 19â€“24, 2024), during the first six days of the Motherâ€™s Day Sale, we spent $31,565.29 and generated $215,841.11 in revenue for a **ROAS of 6.84 and CPA of $92.53.**  
â€¢ This year (Apr 29â€“May 4, 2025), we spent $58,063.39 (+84% YoY) and drove $306,123.38 in revenue (+42% YoY), with a ROAS of 5.27 (-23% YoY) and a CPA of $110.72 (+20% YoY). These figures include late attribution.  
With scaling thus far, we've achieved incremental revenue at reduced efficiency. However, if we push further we would be risking an even lower ROAS and higher CAC and in this case, we would recommend holding steady with spend today or finding a middle ground.  
  
We also don't recommend maintaining elevated budgets after the initial sales phase ends as we expect efficiency to drop dramatically, but will hike back up again over next weekend. Let us know if you are aligned here - or prefer to push forward for topline growth in this time.  
Thanks!  
cc: @Ari Murray @Berkeley Clark @Rahul @User_7DB7H9

In terms of **performance measurement,** Google suggested methods such as a **search lift study (only eligible at a $1000/day budget) and accounting for view-through conversions** among other things, which are outlined in the **â€œHolistic Measurement Frameworkâ€** section of their plan.  
One thing to call out: we may see a **dip in overall account efficiency** by launching this campaign at a $500/day budget or more. Since Demand Gen focuses on **upper-funnel objectives** like awareness and consideration, we **shouldnâ€™t expect it to perform on the same metrics as Search, Shopping, or PMax.** For that reason, we recommend **reporting on Demand Gen performance separately**, as it will likely contribute to downstream conversions across other campaigns or organic channels.

- **2025-05-05 11:09** *Jake Panzer*: Hi @Ingrid, we wanted to share this with you directly before looping in the broader email thread with the Google reps. In short, we don't recommend scaling too much further in this time, given where we are at with efficiency. Often, we find reps try to push the limits of spend, so wanted to share the numbers below:  
  
â€¢ Last year (Apr 19â€“24, 2024), during the first six days of the Motherâ€™s Day Sale, we spent $31,565.29 and generated $215,841.11 in revenue for a **ROAS of 6.84 and CPA of $92.53.**  
â€¢ This year (Apr 29â€“May 4, 2025), we spent $58,063.39 (+84% YoY) and drove $306,123.38 in revenue (+42% YoY), with a ROAS of 5.27 (-23% YoY) and a CPA of $110.72 (+20% YoY). These figures include late attribution.  
With scaling thus far, we've achieved incremental revenue at reduced efficiency. However, if we push further we would be risking an even lower ROAS and higher CAC and in this case, we would recommend holding steady with spend today or finding a middle ground.  
  
We also don't recommend maintaining elevated budgets after the initial sales phase ends as we expect efficiency to drop dramatically, but will hike back up again over next weekend. Let us know if you are aligned here - or prefer to push forward for topline growth in this time.  
Thanks!

- **2025-05-08 15:11** *Jake Panzer* ðŸ’¬ 4 replies: Hi @Ingrid, weâ€™ve connected with our Google reps, Tori and Casey, regarding a preliminary **Demand Gen (YouTube) investment plan.** While their initial recommendation was a $100K/month budget ($3,333/day) to drive statistically significant learnings, we flagged that as outside our scope and asked for a more realistic alternative.  
Theyâ€™ve since shared the attached plan, which outlines a "crawl, walk, run" approach to budget scaling. While our original recommendation was $7,500/month ($250/day), the minimum viable spend in their frameworkâ€”the â€œcrawlâ€ scenarioâ€”is set at **$15K/month ($500/day).** Given this is the **lowest tier that still ensures meaningful learnings,** we believe it makes sense to move forward at that level.  
In terms of **performance measurement,** Google suggested methods such as a **search lift study (only eligible at a $1000/day budget) and accounting for view-through conversions** among other things, which are outlined in the **â€œHolistic Measurement Frameworkâ€** section of their plan.  
One thing to call out: we may see a **dip in overall account efficiency** by launching this campaign at a $500/day budget or more. Since Demand Gen focuses on **upper-funnel objectives** like awareness and consideration, we **shouldnâ€™t expect it to perform on the same metrics as Search, Shopping, or PMax.** For that reason, we recommend **reporting on Demand Gen performance separately**, as it will likely contribute to downstream conversions across other campaigns or organic channels.

- **2025-05-05 11:09** *Jake Panzer*: Hi @Ingrid, we wanted to share this with you directly before looping in the broader email thread with the Google reps. In short, we don't recommend scaling too much further in this time, given where we are at with efficiency. Often, we find reps try to push the limits of spend, so wanted to share the numbers below:  
  
â€¢ Last year (Apr 19â€“24, 2024), during the first six days of the Motherâ€™s Day Sale, we spent $31,565.29 and generated $215,841.11 in revenue for a **ROAS of 6.84 and CPA of $92.53.**  
â€¢ This year (Apr 29â€“May 4, 2025), we spent $58,063.39 (+84% YoY) and drove $306,123.38 in revenue (+42% YoY), with a ROAS of 5.27 (-23% YoY) and a CPA of $110.72 (+20% YoY). These figures include late attribution.  
With scaling thus far, we've achieved incremental revenue at reduced efficiency. However, if we push further we would be risking an even lower ROAS and higher CAC and in this case, we would recommend holding steady with spend today or finding a middle ground.  
  
We also don't recommend maintaining elevated budgets after the initial sales phase ends as we expect efficiency to drop dramatically, but will hike back up again over next weekend. Let us know if you are aligned here - or prefer to push forward for topline growth in this time.  
Thanks!

One thing to call out: we may see a **dip in overall account efficiency** by launching this campaign at a $500/day budget or more. - **2025-05-05 11:09** *User_GR9M7E*: Hi @Ingrid, we wanted to share this with you directly before looping in the broader email thread with the Google reps. In short, we don't recommend scaling too much further in this time, given where we are at with efficiency. Often, we find reps try to push the limits of spend, so wanted to share the numbers below:  
  
â€¢ Last year (Apr 19â€“24, 2024), during the first six days of the Motherâ€™s Day Sale, we spent $31,565.29 and generated $215,841.11 in revenue for a **ROAS of 6.84 and CPA of $92.53.**  
â€¢ This year (Apr 29â€“May 4, 2025), we spent $58,063.39 (+84% YoY) and drove $306,123.38 in revenue (+42% YoY), with a ROAS of 5.27 (-23% YoY) and a CPA of $110.72 (+20% YoY). These figures include late attribution.  
With scaling thus far, we've achieved incremental revenue at reduced efficiency. However, if we push further we would be risking an even lower ROAS and higher CAC and in this case, we would recommend holding steady with spend today or finding a middle ground.  
  
We also don't recommend maintaining elevated budgets after the initial sales phase ends as we expect efficiency to drop dramatically, but will hike back up again over next weekend. Let us know if you are aligned here - or prefer to push forward for topline growth in this time.  
Thanks!

- **2025-05-05 11:09** *User_GR9M7E*: Hi @Ingrid, we wanted to share this with you directly before looping in the broader email thread with the Google reps. In short, we don't recommend scaling too much further in this time, given where we are at with efficiency. Often, we find reps try to push the limits of spend, so wanted to share the numbers below:  
  
â€¢ Last year (Apr 19â€“24, 2024), during the first six days of the Motherâ€™s Day Sale, we spent $31,565.29 and generated $215,841.11 in revenue for a **ROAS of 6.84 and CPA of $92.53.**  
â€¢ This year (Apr 29â€“May 4, 2025), we spent $58,063.39 (+84% YoY) and drove $306,123.38 in revenue (+42% YoY), with a ROAS of 5.27 (-23% YoY) and a CPA of $110.72 (+20% YoY). These figures include late attribution.  
With scaling thus far, we've achieved incremental revenue at reduced efficiency. However, if we push further we would be risking an even lower ROAS and higher CAC and in this case, we would recommend holding steady with spend today or finding a middle ground.  
  
We also don't recommend maintaining elevated budgets after the initial sales phase ends as we expect efficiency to drop dramatically, but will hike back up again over next weekend. Let us know if you are aligned here - or prefer to push forward for topline growth in this time.  
Thanks!

- **2025-05-05 11:09** *Rahul Vithanage*: Hi @Ingrid, we wanted to share this with you directly before looping in the broader email thread with the Google reps. In short, we don't recommend scaling too much further in this time, given where we are at with efficiency. Often, we find reps try to push the limits of spend, so wanted to share the numbers below:  
  
â€¢ Last year (Apr 19â€“24, 2024), during the first six days of the Motherâ€™s Day Sale, we spent $31,565.29 and generated $215,841.11 in revenue for a **ROAS of 6.84 and CPA of $92.53.**  
â€¢ This year (Apr 29â€“May 4, 2025), we spent $58,063.39 (+84% YoY) and drove $306,123.38 in revenue (+42% YoY), with a ROAS of 5.27 (-23% YoY) and a CPA of $110.72 (+20% YoY). These figures include late attribution.  
With scaling thus far, we've achieved incremental revenue at reduced efficiency. However, if we push further we would be risking an even lower ROAS and higher CAC and in this case, we would recommend holding steady with spend today or finding a middle ground.  
  
We also don't recommend maintaining elevated budgets after the initial sales phase ends as we expect efficiency to drop dramatically, but will hike back up again over next weekend. Let us know if you are aligned here - or prefer to push forward for topline growth in this time.  
Thanks!

While our original recommendation was $7,500/month ($250/day), the minimum viable spend in their frameworkâ€”the â€œcrawlâ€ scenarioâ€”is set at **$15K/month ($500/day).** Given this is the **lowest tier that still ensures meaningful learnings,** we believe it makes sense to move forward at that level.  
In terms of **performance measurement,** Google suggested methods such as a **search lift study (only eligible at a $1000/day budget) and accounting for view-through conversions** among other things, which are outlined in the **â€œHolistic Measurement Frameworkâ€** section of their plan.  
One thing to call out: we may see a **dip in overall account efficiency** by launching this campaign at a $500/day budget or more. Since Demand Gen focuses on **upper-funnel objectives** like awareness and consideration, we **shouldnâ€™t expect it to perform on the same metrics as Search, Shopping, or PMax.** For that reason, we recommend **reporting on Demand Gen performance separately**, as it will likely contribute to downstream conversions across other campaigns or organic channels.

- **2025-05-05 11:09** *Rahul Vithanage*: Hi @Ingrid, we wanted to share this with you directly before looping in the broader email thread with the Google reps. In short, we don't recommend scaling too much further in this time, given where we are at with efficiency. Often, we find reps try to push the limits of spend, so wanted to share the numbers below:  
  
â€¢ Last year (Apr 19â€“24, 2024), during the first six days of the Motherâ€™s Day Sale, we spent $31,565.29 and generated $215,841.11 in revenue for a **ROAS of 6.84 and CPA of $92.53.**  
â€¢ This year (Apr 29â€“May 4, 2025), we spent $58,063.39 (+84% YoY) and drove $306,123.38 in revenue (+42% YoY), with a ROAS of 5.27 (-23% YoY) and a CPA of $110.72 (+20% YoY). These figures include late attribution.  
With scaling thus far, we've achieved incremental revenue at reduced efficiency. However, if we push further we would be risking an even lower ROAS and higher CAC and in this case, we would recommend holding steady with spend today or finding a middle ground.  
  
We also don't recommend maintaining elevated budgets after the initial sales phase ends as we expect efficiency to drop dramatically, but will hike back up again over next weekend. Let us know if you are aligned here - or prefer to push forward for topline growth in this time.  
Thanks!

- **2025-05-05 11:09** *Rahul Vithanage*: Hi @Ingrid, we wanted to share this with you directly before looping in the broader email thread with the Google reps. In short, we don't recommend scaling too much further in this time, given where we are at with efficiency. Often, we find reps try to push the limits of spend, so wanted to share the numbers below:  
  
â€¢ Last year (Apr 19â€“24, 2024), during the first six days of the Motherâ€™s Day Sale, we spent $31,565.29 and generated $215,841.11 in revenue for a **ROAS of 6.84 and CPA of $92.53.**  
â€¢ This year (Apr 29â€“May 4, 2025), we spent $58,063.39 (+84% YoY) and drove $306,123.38 in revenue (+42% YoY), with a ROAS of 5.27 (-23% YoY) and a CPA of $110.72 (+20% YoY). These figures include late attribution.  
With scaling thus far, we've achieved incremental revenue at reduced efficiency. However, if we push further we would be risking an even lower ROAS and higher CAC and in this case, we would recommend holding steady with spend today or finding a middle ground.  
  
We also don't recommend maintaining elevated budgets after the initial sales phase ends as we expect efficiency to drop dramatically, but will hike back up again over next weekend. Let us know if you are aligned here - or prefer to push forward for topline growth in this time.  
Thanks!

Theyâ€™ve since shared the attached plan, which outlines a "crawl, walk, run" approach to budget scaling. While our original recommendation was $7,500/month ($250/day), the minimum viable spend in their frameworkâ€”the â€œcrawlâ€ scenarioâ€”is set at **$15K/month ($500/day).** Given this is the **lowest tier that still ensures meaningful learnings,** we believe it makes sense to move forward at that level.  
In terms of **performance measurement,** Google suggested methods such as a **search lift study (only eligible at a $1000/day budget) and accounting for view-through conversions** among other things, which are outlined in the **â€œHolistic Measurement Frameworkâ€** section of their plan.  
One thing to call out: we may see a **dip in overall account efficiency** by launching this campaign at a $500/day budget or more. Since Demand Gen focuses on **upper-funnel objectives** like awareness and consideration, we **shouldnâ€™t expect it to perform on the same metrics as Search, Shopping, or PMax.** For that reason, we recommend **reporting on Demand Gen performance separately**, as it will likely contribute to downstream conversions across other campaigns or organic channels.

- **2025-05-05 11:09** *Rahul Vithanage*: Hi @Ingrid, we wanted to share this with you directly before looping in the broader email thread with the Google reps. In short, we don't recommend scaling too much further in this time, given where we are at with efficiency. Often, we find reps try to push the limits of spend, so wanted to share the numbers below:  
  
â€¢ Last year (Apr 19â€“24, 2024), during the first six days of the Motherâ€™s Day Sale, we spent $31,565.29 and generated $215,841.11 in revenue for a **ROAS of 6.84 and CPA of $92.53.**  
â€¢ This year (Apr 29â€“May 4, 2025), we spent $58,063.39 (+84% YoY) and drove $306,123.38 in revenue (+42% YoY), with a ROAS of 5.27 (-23% YoY) and a CPA of $110.72 (+20% YoY). These figures include late attribution.  
With scaling thus far, we've achieved incremental revenue at reduced efficiency. However, if we push further we would be risking an even lower ROAS and higher CAC and in this case, we would recommend holding steady with spend today or finding a middle ground.  
  
We also don't recommend maintaining elevated budgets after the initial sales phase ends as we expect efficiency to drop dramatically, but will hike back up again over next weekend. Let us know if you are aligned here - or prefer to push forward for topline growth in this time.  
Thanks!
